class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10k-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>The Boeing Company</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/o\xca\x8a/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">o\xca\x8a</span><span title="/\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">\xc9\xaa</span><span title="/\xc5\x8b/: &#39;ng&#39; in &#39;sing&#39;">\xc5\x8b</span></span>/</a></span></span>) is an American <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational corporation</a> that designs, manufactures, and sells <a href="/wiki/Airplane" title="Airplane">airplanes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rotorcraft" title="Rotorcraft">rotorcraft</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rocket" title="Rocket">rockets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">satellites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_equipment" title="Telecommunications equipment">telecommunications equipment</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Missile" title="Missile">missiles</a> worldwide. The company also provides leasing and product support services. Boeing is among the largest global <a href="/wiki/Aerospace_manufacturer" title="Aerospace manufacturer">aerospace manufacturers</a>; it is the second-largest <a href="/wiki/List_of_defense_contractors" title="List of defense contractors">defense contractor</a> in the world based on 2018 revenue,<sup id="cite_ref-DefenseNews_Top_100_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DefenseNews_Top_100-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and is the largest exporter in the United States by dollar value.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Boeing stock is included in the <a href="/wiki/Dow_Jones_Industrial_Average" title="Dow Jones Industrial Average">Dow Jones Industrial Average</a>. Boeing is incorporated in Delaware.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Boeing was founded by <a href="/wiki/William_Boeing" class="mw-redirect" title="William Boeing">William Boeing</a> in <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a> on July 15, 1916.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The present corporation is the result of the merger of Boeing with <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas" title="McDonnell Douglas">McDonnell Douglas</a> on August 1, 1997. Then chairman and CEO of Boeing, <a href="/wiki/Philip_M._Condit" title="Philip M. Condit">Philip M. Condit</a>, assumed those roles in the combined company, while <a href="/wiki/Harry_Stonecipher" title="Harry Stonecipher">Harry Stonecipher</a>, former CEO of McDonnell Douglas, became president and COO.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Boeing Company has its corporate headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-corp_hq_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-corp_hq-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Boeing is organized into four primary divisions: <a href="/wiki/Boeing_Commercial_Airplanes" title="Boeing Commercial Airplanes">Boeing Commercial Airplanes</a> (BCA); <a href="/wiki/Boeing_Defense,_Space_%26_Security" title="Boeing Defense, Space &amp; Security">Boeing Defense, Space &amp; Security</a> (BDS); Boeing Global Services; and <a href="/wiki/Boeing_Capital" title="Boeing Capital">Boeing Capital</a>. In 2019, Boeing recorded <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$</span> 76.6 <span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion in sales. Boeing is ranked 40th on the <i><a href="/wiki/Fortune_(magazine)" title="Fortune (magazine)">Fortune</a></i> magazine "Fortune 500" list (2019),<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> and ranked 121th on the "<a href="/wiki/Fortune_Global_500" title="Fortune Global 500">Fortune Global 500</a>" list (2020).<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2019, Boeing\'s global reputation, commercial business, and financial rating suffered after the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_MAX_groundings" title="Boeing 737 MAX groundings">737 MAX was grounded</a> worldwide following two fatal crashes in <a href="/wiki/Lion_Air_Flight_610" title="Lion Air Flight 610">late 2018</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Airlines_Flight_302" title="Ethiopian Airlines Flight 302">early 2019</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2"><a href="#737_MAX_crashes_and_grounding"><span class="tocnumber">1.1</span> <span class="toctext">737 MAX crashes and grounding</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#Divisions"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Divisions</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4"><a href="#Environmental_record"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Environmental record</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#Jet_biofuels"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Jet biofuels</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6"><a href="#Electric_propulsion"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Electric propulsion</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7"><a href="#Political_contributions,_federal_contracts,_advocacy"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Political contributions, federal contracts, advocacy</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8"><a href="#Criticism"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Criticism</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9"><a href="#Financials"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Financials</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10"><a href="#Employment_numbers"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Employment numbers</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Corporate_governance"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Corporate governance</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Board_of_directors"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Board of directors</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Chief_executive_officer"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Chief executive officer</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Chairman_of_the_board"><span class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">Chairman of the board</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#President"><span class="tocnumber">7.4</span> <span class="toctext">President</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boeing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Boeing" title="History of Boeing">History of Boeing</a></div>\n<p>The Boeing Company was started in 1916, when American lumber industrialist <a href="/wiki/William_E._Boeing" title="William E. Boeing">William E. Boeing</a> founded Aero Products Company in Seattle, Washington. Shortly before doing so, he and Conrad Westervelt created the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_Model_1" title="Boeing Model 1">"B&amp;W" seaplane</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In 1917, the organization was renamed Boeing Airplane Company, with William Boeing forming Boeing Airplane &amp; Transport Corporation in 1928.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> In 1929, the company was renamed <a href="/wiki/United_Aircraft_and_Transport_Corporation" title="United Aircraft and Transport Corporation">United Aircraft and Transport Corporation</a>, followed by the acquisition of several aircraft makers such as Avion, Chance Vought, Sikorsky Aviation, Stearman Aircraft, <a href="/wiki/Pratt_%26_Whitney" title="Pratt &amp; Whitney">Pratt &amp; Whitney</a>, and Hamilton Metalplane.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_Boe_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica_Boe-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1931, the group merged its four smaller airlines into <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a>. In 1934, the manufacture of aircraft was required to be separate from air transportation.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Therefore, Boeing Airplane Company became one of three major groups to arise from dissolution of United Aircraft and Transport; the other two entities were <a href="/wiki/United_Aircraft" title="United Aircraft">United Aircraft</a> (later <a href="/wiki/United_Technologies" title="United Technologies">United Technologies</a>) and United Airlines.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_Boe_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica_Boe-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:2_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1960, the company bought <a href="/wiki/Piasecki_Helicopter" title="Piasecki Helicopter">Vertol Aircraft Corporation</a>, which at the time, was the biggest independent fabricator of <a href="/wiki/Helicopter" title="Helicopter">helicopters</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> During the 1960s and 1970s, the company diversified into industries such as outer space travel, marine craft, agriculture, energy production and transit systems.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_Boe_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica_Boe-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1995, Boeing partnered with Russian, Ukrainian and Anglo-Norwegian organizations to create <a href="/wiki/Sea_Launch" title="Sea Launch">Sea Launch</a>, a company providing commercial launch services sending satellites to geostationary orbit from floating platforms.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In 2000, Boeing acquired the satellite segment of <a href="/wiki/Hughes_Electronics" title="Hughes Electronics">Hughes Electronics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_Boe_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica_Boe-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 1996, Boeing announced its intention to merge with <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas" title="McDonnell Douglas">McDonnell Douglas</a> and, following regulatory approval, this was completed on August 4, 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> This had been delayed by objections from the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>, which ultimately placed 3 conditions on the merger: termination of exclusivity agreements with 3 US airlines, separate accounts would be maintained for the McDonnell-Douglas civil aircraft business, and some defense patents were to be made available to competitors.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The corporate headquarters were moved from Seattle to Chicago in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In 2018, Boeing opened its first factory in Europe at <a href="/wiki/Sheffield" title="Sheffield">Sheffield</a>, UK reinforced by research partnership with <a href="/wiki/The_University_of_Sheffield" class="mw-redirect" title="The University of Sheffield">The University of Sheffield</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 2020, the company cut over 12,000 jobs due to the drop in air travel during the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> with plans for a total 10% cut of its workforce or approximately 16,000 positions.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> In July 2020, Boeing reported a loss of $2.4 billion as a result of the pandemic and the grounding of its 737 MAX aircraft. As a result of the profit loss, the company announced that it is planning to do more job and production cuts.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> On August 18, 2020, CEO Dave Calhoun announced to Boeing employees that the company plans another round of job cuts in addition to the 16,000 positions previously announced to be eliminated.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On October 28, 2020, Boeing CEO David Calhoun, in an email message to employees, announced the lay off nearly 30,000 employees, as the airplane manufacturer was increasingly losing money due to the COVID-19 pandemic.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777X" title="Boeing 777X">Boeing 777X</a>, the largest capacity twinjet, made its maiden flight on January 25, 2020,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> and should enter service in 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-Boeing27jan2021_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boeing27jan2021-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="737_MAX_crashes_and_grounding">737 MAX crashes and grounding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boeing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 737 MAX crashes and grounding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_MAX_groundings" title="Boeing 737 MAX groundings">Boeing 737 MAX groundings</a></div>\n<p>After two fatal crashes of the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_MAX" title="Boeing 737 MAX">Boeing 737 MAX</a> narrow-body passenger airplanes in 2018 and 2019, aviation regulators and airlines around the world <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_MAX_groundings" title="Boeing 737 MAX groundings">grounded all 737 MAX</a> airliners.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> A total of 387 aircraft were grounded.<sup id="cite_ref-:10_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:10-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Boeing\'s reputation, business, and financial rating has suffered after these groundings, questioning Boeing\'s strategy, governance, and focus on profits and cost efficiency.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Divisions">Divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boeing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ridley_Park_PA_Boeing.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Boeing plant in Ridley Park, Pennsylvania \xe2\x80\x93 a building with aluminum siding, parking lot in front, and a flagpole with seven flags" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Ridley_Park_PA_Boeing.JPG/220px-Ridley_Park_PA_Boeing.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Ridley_Park_PA_Boeing.JPG/330px-Ridley_Park_PA_Boeing.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Ridley_Park_PA_Boeing.JPG/440px-Ridley_Park_PA_Boeing.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3860" data-file-height="2573" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ridley_Park_PA_Boeing.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Boeing plant in <a href="/wiki/Ridley_Park,_Pennsylvania" title="Ridley Park, Pennsylvania">Ridley Park, Pennsylvania</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The corporation\'s three main divisions are Boeing Commercial Airplanes (BCA), Boeing Defense, Space &amp; Security (BDS), and Boeing Global Services.<sup id="cite_ref-Brief_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brief-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Boeing_Commercial_Airplanes" title="Boeing Commercial Airplanes">Boeing Commercial Airplanes</a> (BCA)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Boeing_Defense,_Space_%26_Security" title="Boeing Defense, Space &amp; Security">Boeing Defense, Space &amp; Security</a> (BDS)\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Boeing_Phantom_Works" title="Boeing Phantom Works">Phantom Works</a></li></ul></li>\n<li>Boeing Global Services</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Boeing_Capital" title="Boeing Capital">Boeing Capital</a></li>\n<li>Engineering, Test &amp; Technology</li>\n<li>Boeing Shared Services Group</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Boeing_NeXt" title="Boeing NeXt">Boeing NeXt</a> \xe2\x80\x93 explores <a href="/wiki/Urban_air_mobility" title="Urban air mobility">urban air mobility</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_record">Environmental record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boeing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Environmental record">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In 2006, the <a href="/wiki/UCLA" class="mw-redirect" title="UCLA">UCLA</a> Center for Environmental Risk Reduction released a study showing that Boeing\'s <a href="/wiki/Santa_Susana_Field_Laboratory" title="Santa Susana Field Laboratory">Santa Susana Field Laboratory</a>, a site that was a former Rocketdyne test and development site in the <a href="/wiki/Simi_Hills" title="Simi Hills">Simi Hills</a> of eastern <a href="/wiki/Ventura_County" class="mw-redirect" title="Ventura County">Ventura County</a> in <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a>, had been contaminated by Rocketdyne with <a href="/wiki/Toxic" class="mw-redirect" title="Toxic">toxic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Radioactive_waste" title="Radioactive waste">radioactive waste</a>. Boeing agreed to a cleanup agreement with the EPA in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Clean up studies and lawsuits are in progress.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jet_biofuels">Jet biofuels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boeing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Jet biofuels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Aviation_biofuel" title="Aviation biofuel">Aviation biofuel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Algae_fuel" title="Algae fuel">Algae fuel</a></div>\n<p>The airline industry is responsible for about 11% of <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gases</a> emitted by the U.S. transportation sector.<sup id="cite_ref-boe_energy_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boe_energy-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Aviation\'s share of the greenhouse gas emissions was poised to grow, as air travel increases and ground vehicles use more alternative fuels like ethanol and biodiesel.<sup id="cite_ref-boe_energy_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boe_energy-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Boeing estimates that biofuels could reduce flight-related greenhouse-gas emissions by 60 to 80%.<sup id="cite_ref-boe_energy_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boe_energy-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The solution blends algae fuels with existing <a href="/wiki/Jet_fuel" title="Jet fuel">jet fuel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-boe_energy_38-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boe_energy-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Boeing executives said the company was collaborating with Brazilian biofuels maker <a href="/wiki/Tecbio" class="mw-redirect" title="Tecbio">Tecbio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aquaflow_Bionomic" class="mw-redirect" title="Aquaflow Bionomic">Aquaflow Bionomic</a> of New Zealand, and other fuel developers around the world. As of 2007, Boeing had tested six fuels from these companies, and expected to test 20 fuels "by the time we\'re done evaluating them".<sup id="cite_ref-boe_energy_38-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boe_energy-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Boeing also joined other aviation-related members in the <a href="/wiki/Algal_Biomass_Organization" class="mw-redirect" title="Algal Biomass Organization">Algal Biomass Organization</a> (ABO) in June 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Air_New_Zealand" title="Air New Zealand">Air New Zealand</a> and Boeing are researching the <a href="/wiki/Jatropha" title="Jatropha">jatropha</a> plant to see if it is a sustainable alternative to conventional fuel.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> A two-hour test flight using a 50\xe2\x80\x9350 mixture of the new biofuel with <a href="/wiki/Jet_fuel" title="Jet fuel">Jet A-1</a> in a Rolls Royce RB-211 engine of a 747-400 was completed on December 30, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The engine was then removed to be studied to identify any differences between the Jatropha blend and regular Jet A1. No effects on performances were found.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On August 31, 2010, Boeing worked with the U.S. Air Force to test the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_C-17" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing C-17">Boeing C-17</a> running on 50% JP-8, 25% Hydro-treated Renewable Jet fuel and 25% of a Fischer\xe2\x80\x93Tropsch fuel with successful results.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electric_propulsion">Electric propulsion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boeing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Electric propulsion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>For NASA\'s N+3 future airliner program, Boeing has determined that <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_vehicle" title="Hybrid electric vehicle">hybrid electric</a> engine technology is by far the best choice for its subsonic design. Hybrid electric propulsion has the potential to shorten takeoff distance and reduce noise. Boeing created a team to study electric propulsion in future generation of subsonic commercial aircraft.&#160;SUGAR for Subsonic Ultra Green Aircraft Research includes, BR&amp;T, Boeing Commercial Airplanes, General Electric, and Georgia Tech. There are five main concepts of the team is reviewing. SUGAR Free and Refined SUGAR, are two concepts based on conventional aircraft similar to the 737. SUGAR High and SUGAR Volt, are both high span, strut-based wing concepts. The final concept is SUGAR Ray, which is a wing body hybrid. The SUGAR Volt concept has resulted in a drop in fuel burn of more than 70 percent and a reduction of total energy use by 55 percent. This reduction is the result of adding an electric battery gas turbine hybrid propulsion system.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Political_contributions.2C_federal_contracts.2C_advocacy"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_contributions,_federal_contracts,_advocacy">Political contributions, federal contracts, advocacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boeing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Political contributions, federal contracts, advocacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_787-10_rollout_with_President_Trump_(32335755473)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Boeing_787-10_rollout_with_President_Trump_%2832335755473%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Boeing_787-10_rollout_with_President_Trump_%2832335755473%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Boeing_787-10_rollout_with_President_Trump_%2832335755473%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Boeing_787-10_rollout_with_President_Trump_%2832335755473%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3172" data-file-height="2119" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_787-10_rollout_with_President_Trump_(32335755473)_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Boeing CEO <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Muilenburg" title="Dennis Muilenburg">Dennis Muilenburg</a> and President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Trump</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">787-10 Dreamliner</a> rollout ceremony in 2017</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2008 and 2009, Boeing was second on the list of <a href="/wiki/Top_100_US_Federal_Contractors" class="mw-redirect" title="Top 100 US Federal Contractors">Top 100 US Federal Contractors</a>, with contracts totaling <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$</span>22&#160;billion and <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$</span>23&#160;billion respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>  Between 1995 and early 2021, the company has agreed to pay <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$</span>4.3&#160;billion to settle 84 instances of misconduct, including <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$</span>615&#160;million in 2006 in relation to illegal hiring of government officials and improper use of proprietary information.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Boeing secured the highest ever <a href="/wiki/Tax_break" title="Tax break">tax breaks</a> at the state level in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Boeing\'s spent <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$</span>16.9&#160;million on lobbying expenditures in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/2008_United_States_presidential_election" title="2008 United States presidential election">2008 presidential election</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> "was by far the biggest recipient of campaign contributions from Boeing employees and executives, hauling in <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$</span>197,000 \xe2\x80\x93 five times as much as <a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">John McCain</a>, and more than the top eight Republicans combined".<sup id="cite_ref-Carney_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carney-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Boeing has a <a href="/wiki/Corporate_citizenship" class="mw-redirect" title="Corporate citizenship">corporate citizenship</a> program centered on charitable contributions in five areas: <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education</a>, <a href="/wiki/Health" title="Health">health</a>, <a href="/wiki/Human_services" title="Human services">human services</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natural_environment" title="Natural environment">environment</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_arts" title="The arts">the arts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">culture</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Civics" title="Civics">civic engagement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (September 2012)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In 2011, Boeing spent <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$</span>147.3&#160;million in these areas through <a href="/wiki/Charity_(practice)" title="Charity (practice)">charitable grants</a> and <a href="/wiki/Patronage" title="Patronage">business sponsorships</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>  In February 2012, Boeing Global Corporate Citizenship partnered with the <a href="/wiki/Insight_Labs" title="Insight Labs">Insight Labs</a> to develop a new model for <a href="/wiki/Foundation_(non-profit)" class="mw-redirect" title="Foundation (non-profit)">foundations</a> to more effectively lead the sectors they serve.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (September 2012)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The company is a member of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Global_Leadership_Coalition" title="U.S. Global Leadership Coalition">U.S. Global Leadership Coalition</a>, a Washington D.C.-based coalition of more than 400 major companies and NGOs that advocate a larger International Affairs Budget, which funds American diplomatic and development efforts abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> A series of <a href="/wiki/US_diplomatic_cables_release" class="mw-redirect" title="US diplomatic cables release">U.S. diplomatic cables</a> show how U.S. diplomats and senior politicians intervene on behalf of Boeing to help boost the company\'s sales.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2007 and 2008, the company benefited from over <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$</span>10&#160;billion of long-term loan guarantees, helping finance the purchase of their commercial aircraft in countries including Brazil, Canada, Ireland, and the United Arab Emirates, from the <a href="/wiki/Export-Import_Bank_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Export-Import Bank of the United States">Export-Import Bank of the United States</a>, some 65% of the total loan guarantees the bank made in the period.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boeing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In December 2011, the non-partisan organization <a href="/wiki/Public_Campaign#Reports" class="mw-redirect" title="Public Campaign">Public Campaign</a> criticized Boeing for spending <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$</span>52.29&#160;million on <a href="/wiki/Lobbying" title="Lobbying">lobbying</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tax_avoidance" title="Tax avoidance">not paying taxes</a> during 2008\xe2\x80\x932010, instead getting <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$</span>178&#160;million in tax rebates, despite making a profit of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$</span>9.7&#160;billion, laying off 14,862 workers since 2008, and increasing executive pay by 31% to <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$</span>41.9&#160;million in 2010 for its top five executives.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The firm has also been criticized for supplying and profiting from wars, including the war in Yemen where its missiles were found to be used for indiscriminate attacks, killing many civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Boeing has been accused of unethical practices (in violation of the <a href="/wiki/Procurement_Integrity_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Procurement Integrity Act">Procurement Integrity Act</a>) while attempting to submit a revised bid to NASA for lunar landing project.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Financials">Financials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boeing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Financials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td Boeing\'s shares traded at over $209 per share, and its market capitalization was valued at over <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$</span>206.6<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable float-left" style="text-align: right;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Year\n</th>\n<th>Revenue <br />in million US$\n</th>\n<th>Net (Loss)/Earnings <br />in mil. href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Between 2010 and 2018, Boeing increased its operating <a href="/wiki/Cash_flow" title="Cash flow">cash flow</a> from $3 to $15.3<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion, sustaining its <a href="/wiki/Share_(finance)" title="Share (finance)">share</a> price, by negotiating <a href="/wiki/Advance_payment" title="Advance payment">advance payments</a> from customers and delaying payments to its suppliers. This strategy is sustainable only as long as orders are good and delivery rates are increasing.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From 2013 to 2019, Boeing spent over $60 billion on dividends and <a href="/wiki/Share_repurchase" title="Share repurchase">stock buybacks</a>, twice as much as the development costs of the 787.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Employment_numbers">Employment numbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boeing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Employment numbers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The company\'s employment totals are listed below.\n</p>\n<div>\n\n&#32;\n<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: right;">141,014\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n<p>Approximately 1.5% of Boeing employees are in the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_Technical_Fellowship" title="Boeing Technical Fellowship">Technical Fellowship</a> program, a program through which Boeing\'s top engineers and scientists set technical direction for the company.<sup id="cite_ref-techfellow_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-techfellow-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> The average salary at Boeing is $76,784, reported by former employees.<sup
